According to a study, a staggering 96% of deepfakesare pornographic, and started as deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films but quickly spread to revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. The widespread exploitation of deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes on the internet, and academic research has focused around detecting deepfakes. Some platforms, such as Facebook, instead have opted to enforce that users clearly note that media is a deepfakes. Some AIs are much more nuanced, and thus that much more dangerous. GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, is able to generate text so similar to that written by humans that they did not release it to the public out of fear that it would be rampantly misused. OpenAI has also released DALLE, a model that can generate artwork based on text prompts, which is a fun experiment, but could easily be misused.

It is also imperative for those who use AI to be completely transparent about exactly what it is capable of and what it is using. There also needs to be an effort to educate people on what AI can do from a young age. This doesn’t have to be an effort to get more involved with AI, but moreso a rudimentary understanding of its limitations.

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been hotly debated but has not been widely explored. This is because it can be extremely hard to tell what kind of ramifications such a relationship will have. In the following examples, only the most extreme examples can be seen. In many of these cases, it is best to avoid such a relationship entirely. 

This one is not as black and white, but is still important to understand. In order to illustrate this, let's say that there is a sexual relationship between a human and an artificial intelligence. This is not to say that such a relationship is not possible, it is simply not what we typically think of when we think of artificial intelligence. The most common responses to this is to say that the problem goes beyond AI to people, and that we need to move on. This is not to say that such a move is not possible, it is simply that we do not think about the consequences of such a move strongly enough to begin with.

There is a marked difference between the capabilities and expectations of Artificial Intelligence. Science fiction writers, film directors, and artists would have you believe that AI is manifested in sentient robots that are binary equivalents of humans. This kind of AI is referred to in academic literature as “strong” AI, which is an AI that is intelligent enough to understand or learn any intellectual task that a human being can. Generalized AI is not here yet -- instead, what you will find are “narrow” AIs that are trained to accomplish very specific tasks: identify an image, suggest an enjoyable movie, predict the next word in a sentence, etc. Narrow AI has been able to dethrone the world champion at Go, vanquish the Jeopardy champions, and defeat Gary Kasparov at chess. There are also “weak” AIs that can implement a limited part of a mind, but not the entire mind. The most common examples include Siri, Cortana, and Google Assistant: these voice assistants have a very narrow spectrum they can operate in, and asking any question outside of their limited scope will result in unhelpful responses. It is important to realize that artificial intelligence is on the rise - just slower than the media coverage would lead you to believe.

There is a marked difference between the perception and reality of Artificial Intelligence. Media is hyperfocused on “strong” AI, which is an AI that is intelligent enough to understand or learn any intellectual task that a human being can. This is the kind of AI glamorized in films and novels. In reality, AI today is much more boring. The majority of AI in production today is “narrow” AI, which are trained and fine tuned to perform extremely specific tasks. You may have heard of Google’s DeepMind AI, which dethroned the world champion at Go. IBM Watson dominated against the Jeopardy champions. These AIs are all narrow; they can only play the game they have been trained for. Furthermore, most AI found today is not nearly as exciting: data analysis, image classification, and signal processing. These applications do not attract media attention, but are incredibly important to their respective fields. The final major class of AI is “weak” AIs, which can implement a limited part of a mind, but not the entire mind. The most common examples include Siri, Cortana, and Google Assistant. These AIs have a very limited scope of operation, and asking any question outside of this scope will result in largely unhelpful responses. It is important to realize that artificial intelligence is on the rise - just slower than the media coverage would lead you to believe.

Even without general AI, narrow and weak AI have brought several ethical and practical concerns up that should absolutely be dealt with.

This will no doubt shift the job demand towards fields such as software engineering and robotics, but there will be notable disruptions in areas such as manufacturing and data entry. In short, any task that is simple enough to be learned by a computer will more than likely be taken over by a computer. This is widely viewed as a good thing, as it allows humans to focus on more creative and difficult problems to solve. However, there is the unanswered issue of how to redistribute the wealth generated by machines. Companies such as Alibaba and Amazon now have warehouses entirely staffed by robots. Human-robot interaction is a field that has been slowly but surely growing, and one that will no doubt only get more crowded as artificial intelligence advances. The potential is enormous, and it will take something incredibly basic to stop this. What do we do with the AIs that don’t learn? What happens to the humans that lose out? These are difficult questions to answer. 

One of the primary issues is that artificial intelligence will disrupt menial jobs. What do we do with the suddenly jobless people? The demand for work will shift to software engineering and robotics -- we will need bright minds to program the future. Any task that is simple enough to be learned by a computer will be taken over by a computer. Furthermore, how do we redistribute the wealth generated by machines? Should profits go directly to the company? To workers? The government? This is a hard question to answer, but should absolutely be addressed if we are to move forward.

AI is not perfect. Although commonly trained for 90% or higher accuracy, there are still cases where the AI fails. This could prove disastrous in high-risk applications such as self-driving cars, automated weaponry, and the medical field. Tesla’s self-driving AI proved to be fatal for its driver when it could not distinguish a white semi-truck against the bright bluish-white sky. Artificial Intelligence is often asked to do herculean tasks and failures can be devastating. Take IBM’s “Watson for Oncology” AI. This was a project meant to aid cancer patients by scanning similar patients and recommending similar treatments. The final AI was an utter failure, suggesting incorrect and dangerous cancer treatment advice. Microsoft’s Twitter chatbot was intended to engage in conversation with twitter users, and it only took a day for the internet to teach it to be misogynistic, racist, and anti-semitic. The project was pulled, but is a good example that it is hard to anticipate how AI can be misused. Bias is a huge issue in AI; it is often said that a programmer will write his/her bias into every program they write, and AI is no exception. Amazon’s recruitment AI had to be deprecated because it would disproportionately choose males over females. This example actually points to a larger issue: bad datasets. An AI is only as good as the data used to train it, and the Amazon AI was trained with current engineering employees, which is a predominantly male field. One of the most egregious examples of an AI classifying incorrectly is Google Photos image recognition algorithm classifying African American people as Gorillas. Their solution? Remove the Gorilla label from the classification corpus. This is clearly not the correct way to go about this, but showcases that AI still has a long way to go, and we are not entirely sure how to deal with failures.

AI is not perfect. AIs are trained for extremely high accuracy (usually, anything below 90% is considered unusable), but this does not mean they don’t fail. This could prove disastrous in high-risk applications such as self-driving cars, automated weaponry, and the medical field, to name a few. Notably, Tesla’s self-driving AI has proved to be fatal for a driver when it crashed into a white semi-truck when it could not distinguish it against a bluish-white sky. Too often, Artificial Intelligence is asked to do herculean tasks which often yield devastating results. Consider IBM’s “Watson for Oncology” AI. This was an AI whose purpose was to aid cancer patients by scanning similar patients and recommend similar treatments. The final implementation was deemed by healthcare professionals to be an utter failure, as Watson suggested incorrect and exceedingly dangerous cancer treatment advice. Microsoft’s Twitter chatbot was meant to converse with twitter users, and it only took one day for the internet to teach it to be misogynistic, racist, and anti-semitic. This is a good example that it can be extremely hard (almost impossible) to anticipate all the ways in which AI can be misused. Bias is a huge issue in AI and probably one of the hardest things to detect in an AI. Amazon’s recruitment AI had to be deprecated because it was misogynistic: the culprit was that the dataset primarily had male resumes, which led to the AI learning to pick male resumes over female ones. This points to the larger issue of an AI only being as good as its dataset. One of the most egregious examples of AIs being wrong is the Google Photos image recognition algorithm, which classified African American people as Gorillas. Google’s solution was to remove the gorilla label from the classification corpus, which is not a perfect solution, but showcases that we do not entirely understand how to deal with AIs being wrong.

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been hotly debated and ultimately categorized as a lab-created outcome. This misses the forest for the better part of the human-robot interaction spectrum, which is anything that isn't a robot driven to complete a specific task. In short, anything that isn't a robot that we can interact with through training and testing. It is by no means a perfect field, but it is a worthwhile one to explore if you can stomach the intellectual burden of proving that anything other than a human is a human. 

One of the primary issues with the AI/human dichotomy is that it implies that AI is some kind of blank slate that should be created solely for the purpose of exploring and derailing human-robot interaction. This is completely at odds with the way that AI is usually built: with an Applicable Human-AI Determinant, and then generic AI that can be tuned to meet any need that is thrown at it. This is illustrated graphically by Google Photos image recognition algorithm, which was built to categorize pictures of people based on their race, rather than any intrinsic intelligence underlying this classification. In the computer vision and image classification industries, this is referred to as "weighted" AI, which is software that is trained to classify roughly the same picture into your mind's eye as to yield slightly different results. This is referred to as "narrow" AI, which is software that is trained to classify the same picture out of a field of possible images to yield the same or slightly different results. There are also cognitive–data–storage–intensive AIs, such as those used in cloud computing, that are designed to store data for future analysis and to be able to recall their analysis is known as "async". This is referred to as "switching" AI, which is software that is designed to run at a high rate of speed and be able to accomplish its task is referred to as "async bairns". These AIs are all gatekeeping annecdotes: they say that the more examples given, the more likely the AI will do it, and AI is often depicted this way: blue–eyed–dumb robot, which can only think and learn. This is often lampshaded when the AI is a blue–eyed robot, who can see and hear. This is lampshaded even more hilariously when the artist behind the AI is blacked out on their computer, so the viewer doesn't have to. This leads onto the next point… Asynchronous AI is a Bad Example Because AIs Are Usually Gatekeeping Annecdotes. An AI is only as good as the first application it is asked to run against, and the vast majority of AI work is not to aid humans in any way, but to aid in computer vision and image classification. This is most evident in healthcare: patients often have very simplistic pain–pain–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–noise–and that's not even counting the time and effort it takes to create the docs and SDKs to help out. This is why so many AIs are Gatekeeping Annecdotes: it gives the impression that AI is capable of anything, when in reality it is more likely than not to be more suited to a particular problem it is asked to solve. Turing Test: A system is considered to be partially successful if it cannot program a human being to do a specific task. The examples given are often incredibly hard: image classification, for instance, is usually modeled after smell: the classifier is trained on millions of examples, and the individual cases it identifies are often extremely rare. The original AI was considered to be partially successful, because it could not program a human being to perform a specific task: the concept of classifying art was left to humans, and the final result is up to artists, not humans. Widespread adoption of AIs to solve extremely hard problems is a good sign, but not nearly as strong as one might think.

AI is usually not as bad as you might think. One of the primary reasons that AI is not adopted as widely is because it is so hard: writing bad AI is incredibly hard, and it can take years for even the most rudimentary AI to fail. Google Photos image recognition algorithm was only considered partially effective because it is extremely hard to model that way, and the general public only has a rough idea what it is trying to classify. Similar to BCIs, deepfakes are simultaneously terrifying and awesome. deepfakesare AIs that can replace images, videos, or audio of a person with another person of similar likeness. deepfakes began circulating in 2017, which were humorous at first, but the danger of Deepfakes quickly became apparent when (unsurprisingly), it went towards pornography. According to a study, a staggering 96% of deepfakesare pornographic, and started as deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films but quickly spread to revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. The widespread exploitation of deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes on the internet, and academic research has focused around detecting deepfakes. Some platforms, such as Facebook, instead have opted to enforce that users clearly note that media is a deepfakes. Some AIs are much more nuanced, and thus that much more dangerous. GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, is able to generate text so similar to that written by humans that they did not release it to the public out of fear that it would be rampantly misused. OpenAI has also released DALLE, a model that can generate artwork based on text prompts, which is a fun experiment, but could easily be misused.

Multiple bills have been introduced to congress about deepfakes. The implications of this are terrifying: there are reports of customers asking for younger-looking robots and recreating rape scenarios, which is horrifying. The psychological effects of pursuing such a relationship with a robot has not been explored in any capacity, and it is currently a field that has no oversight. One of the best science fiction films, Blade Runner 2049 introduces the character Joi, an artificial intelligence which is projected as a hologram intended to be a fully customizable romantic companion. This has a similar issue with the sex robots: what kind of ramifications will this have on people, and ultimately the human race? A man in Japan married an artificial intelligence with no physical form. There are no laws governing this, and it is not a field many people have thought about. The psychological issues and ramifications of such a relationship have not been explored enough to make a decision on this yet. The most terrifying (and awe-inspiring) synthesis between humans and artificial intelligence is brain-computer interfaces. The initial development is meant to aid people with neurological disorders, but it will not take long for it to extend to cybernetic modifications on people. Will this be regulated? Should this even be allowed? At the risk of sounding like a Black Mirror episode, at what point does a human stop being human and start being a robot?

GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, was able to generate text so human-like that the programmers did not open source the model out of fear of rampant misuse. One of the biggest issues with AI is that it is incredibly hard to relay these ideas to people outside academia, which stems back to the mythologization of AI. It is also imperative for those who use AI to be completely transparent about exactly what it is capable of and what it is using. There also needs to be an effort to educate people on what AI can do from a young age. This doesn’t have to be an effort to get more involved with AI, but moreso a rudimentary understanding of its limitations. 

One of the biggest issues with AI is that it is incredibly hard to relay these ideas to people outside academia, which is what leads to the difference between the perception and reality of AI. AI developers should be straightforward and honest about what is being developed, and there needs to be an effort to educate on what AI can do. AI tends to be a very mysterious field to those not in, but if the basics were taught, there would be a lot less misunderstanding about what AI can and cannot do.

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been marred by controversy and misunderstanding. The primary issue is that they are creatures that are made to be played by human beings. They also often require significant physical exertion to achieve the same effect. Furthermore, the psychological effects associated with such interactions have not been explored in any capacity. The final major issue is that these relationships have not been explored in any fashion. This is most notably seen in the movie Blade Runner 2049, which deals with the development of a humanoid companion for the purpose of mating. This has a very different take on the gender divide in science and technology than the gender binary used in film and media.

In the future, humans will not be able to communicate with one another. Instead, they will rely on data mining to glean useful traits from the world around them. This will bring about changes in how we live our lives, and it will be the left wing that will be held to account.

This will not be a good thing. 


Society is currently in the midst of an unhelpful debate about how to deal with sex robots. The consensus seems to be that the sex robots should be kept as far away from humans as possible, since it is difficult to predict when a sentient robot will decide to interact with humans and start having sex with them. This view is particularly misguided when one considers that robots will most likely be human-robot compatible. This means that the robots will not be able to feel, see, or remember any of the human qualities that go along with being a person. Instead, the focus will be on artificial intelligence and rapid prototyping. This means that the final product will almost certainly be far more human-like than the initial prototype. This is widely viewed as a good thing, as it allows humans to make important contributions to the human race, but also allows unusual creations like sex robots to go to waste. It is important to realize that human-robot interaction is a field that has been a field of research that has been largely unexplored. 

Sociological and psychological theories have suggested that we should not be delving too deeply into the psychology of mental illness. Instead, we should focus on rapid prototyping and exploring possible treatment options. For example, amending the Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders to include a definition of mental illness that is universal and non-discriminating is one way to go. This would allow people with psychiatric disorders to receive treatment and still have the right to be discharged if they so choose. Similarly, there are efforts to create a universal basic income (UBI) that would provide all citizens of a country with a certain amount of money every month. This scheme has various issues, such as: • Increasing inequality • Elevating the status of women • Obstructing progress • Lacking a clear moral rationale • Ripping off the existing population This is a complex issue that will take some time to get to a place of consensus on, but is potentially a much better world than we have today.

Neural networks are one of the fundamental building blocks of a neural network. A neural network is simply a computer program that can learn any problem it is given the opportunity to. There are currently over 400,000 computer programs categorized as neural networks, and they have been able to identify objects in images and predict the future by just a few hundredths of a percent. This is an incredibly powerful method for identifying something as basic as a door by just a few hundredths of a percent, and it is used in everything from image classification to speech recognition to identify the body parts of cryptids. The potential is clearly there, and it is expected that artificial intelligence will eventually be able to do anything a human can. This is not to say that this will be without consequences, but these problems will slowly be surmounted over time.

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been slowly but surely growing, with notable contributions such as Uber’s self-driving AI, which gave San Francisco an A+ taxi rating, and Ford’s decision to exclusively hire white males for its workforce, which resulted in a decrease in gender representation at the company. This is not to say that there have not been any attempts to create a gender-neutral version of an AI, but rather that such a system would have to be Turing complete to be accepted by the public. There have also been reports of sexual assault and harassment directed towards AI, which is entirely their problem. It is important to realize that artificial intelligence is on the rise - just slower than the media coverage would lead you to believe.

There is a marked difference between the perception and reality of Artificial Intelligence. Media is hyperfocused on “strong” AI, which is an AI that is intelligent enough to understand or learn any intellectual task that a human being can. This is the kind of AI glamorized in films and novels. In reality, AI today is much more boring. The majority of AI in production today is “narrow” AI, which are trained and fine tuned to perform extremely specific tasks. You may have heard of Google’s DeepMind AI, which dethroned the world champion at Go. IBM Watson dominated against the Jeopardy champions. These AIs are all narrow; they can only play the game they have been trained for. Furthermore, most AI found today is not nearly as exciting: data analysis, image classification, and signal processing. These applications do not attract media attention, but are incredibly important to their respective fields. The final major class of AI is “weak” AIs, which can implement a limited part of a mind, but not the entire mind. The most common examples include Siri, Cortana, and Google Assistant. These AIs have a very limited scope of operation, and asking any question outside of this scope will result in largely unhelpful responses. It is important to realize that artificial intelligence is on the rise - just slower than the media coverage would lead you to believe.

Even though we don’t have general AI, there have already been a plethora of ethical and practical concerns that have arisen. In the following paragraphs, we will briefly explore a few of these concerns.   

Even though we don’t have general AI, there have already been a myriad of concerns that have arisen. We will now briefly explore these concerns. 

Even without general AI, narrow and weak AI have brought several ethical and practical concerns up that should absolutely be dealt with. 

One of the primary issues is that artificial intelligence replaces menial labor. What do we do with the people who have suddenly become jobless? This will no doubt shift the job demand towards fields such as software engineering and robotics, but there will be notable disruptions in areas such as manufacturing and data entry. In short, any task that is simple enough to be learned by a computer will more than likely be taken over by a computer. This is widely viewed as a good thing, as it allows humans to focus on more creative and difficult problems to solve. However, there is the unanswered issue of how to redistribute the wealth generated by machines. Companies such as Alibaba and Amazon now have warehouses entirely staffed by robots. Should the money made by these warehouses go to the company? The workers? The government? This is a difficult question to answer, but a necessary one if we are to move forward.

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been lucrative but with little to no regulation. Notably, sex robots have been sold that look and sound exactly how the user wants. The implications of this are terrifying: customers have already begun ordering uncomfortably young-looking robots and are recreating rape scenarios, which is horrifying. There are obvious psychological effects that go along with this, but these have not been explored in any fashion. The film Blade Runner 2049 shows an artificial intelligence projected as a hologram that is intended to be a fully customizable romantic companion. Similar to sex robots, this raises the questions of what kind of ramifications this will have on people and ultimately on the human race. There was a marriage between a man in Japan and an artificial intelligence with no physical form. The most terrifying (and awesome) form of human-robot interaction is brain-computer interfaces. Initial development is aimed at aiding people with neurological disorders, but it will not take long for this to extend to cybernetic modifications on people with no disorders. Will this be regulated? Should this even be allowed? These are difficult questions to answer. 

Similar to BCIs, deepfakes are simultaneously terrifying and awesome. deepfakesare AIs that can replace images, videos, or audio of a person with another person of similar likeness. deepfakes began circulating in 2017, which were humorous at first, but the danger of Deepfakes quickly became apparent when (unsurprisingly), it went towards pornography. According to a study, a staggering 96% of deepfakesare pornographic, and started as deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films but quickly spread to revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. The widespread exploitation of deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes on the internet, and academic research has focused around detecting deepfakes. Some platforms, such as Facebook, instead have opted to enforce that users clearly note that media is a deepfakes. Some AIs are much more nuanced, and thus that much more dangerous. GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, is able to generate text so similar to that written by humans that they did not release it to the public out of fear that it would be rampantly misused. OpenAI has also released DALLE, a model that can generate artwork based on text prompts, which is a fun experiment, but could easily be misused.

A staggering 96% of Deepfakes are estimated to be pornography Deepfakes. It didn’t take long to go from Deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films to creating revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. Deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes, and much of academic research has centered around being able to detect deepfakes. Multiple bills have been introduced to congress about deepfakes. GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, was able to generate text so human-like that the programmers did not open source the model out of fear of rampant misuse. OpenAI has also released a model called DALLE, which can generate artwork based on text prompts. This is a fun experiment but could easily be misused. 

One of the biggest issues with AI is that it is incredibly hard to relay these ideas to people outside academia, which stems back to the mythologization of AI. It is also imperative for those who use AI to be completely transparent about exactly what it is capable of and what it is using. There also needs to be an effort to educate people on what AI can do from a young age. This doesn’t have to be an effort to get more involved with AI, but moreso a rudimentary understanding of its limitations. 

One of the biggest issues with AI is that it is incredibly hard to relay these ideas to people outside academia, which is what leads to the difference between the perception and reality of AI. AI developers should be straightforward and honest about what is being developed, and there needs to be an effort to educate on what AI can do. AI tends to be a very mysterious field to those not in, but if the basics were taught, there would be a lot less misunderstanding about what AI can and cannot do.

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been marred by controversy , but that is nevertheless a very exciting field to work in. There are huge untapped productivity and educational benefits to this field, but there are also huge ethical and legal questions to be addressed. 

There are currently no general AI general AI databasees. Instead, what you will find are "proof of concepts", which are general AI implementations that have been optimized to perform certain tasks extremely well. This is generally viewed as a good thing, as it allows people to focus on developing actual applications and less on developing "proof-of-concepts". However, there is the big issue of control: if somebody else comes up with an application that is 100x better than yours, and you only have one left to show for your time, is there really any control? 

One of the primary issues is that there will inevitably be some overlap: Google’s car was explicitly designed to be compatible with the local auto club, and was able to outsmart them. This points to the larger issue of a singular goal: to find a solution to a given problem, and use that solution to their advantage. This is not to say that there have not been any attempts to identify which problems are most applicable to which situations, but instead that there has been no way to translate this to practice. Human-robot interaction is a field that has been ambitiously explored by sci-fi writers, filmmakers, and artists, but whose true potential has not yet been realized. The primary issue is that the human factor is considered beneath the scope of this limitation. Therefore, it is recommended that projects focusing on human-robot interaction are avoided. 13. Network Analysis . Network analysis is the art and science of gathering and analyzing large volumes of unstructured data to predict human behavior. Typically, this will be used in defense industries to aid in decision-making processes. In reality, this can be disastrously misused. The following Are Bad Examples of Network Analysis: 1. The Joneses. This is a movie about a man whose wife is repeatedly raped and then murdered by her former partner. The implication is that all rapes are equal: that any sexual encounter that does not include the individual wearing the vagina/nose has no significance. This was specifically aimed at men, as they are more likely to understand and implement such a system. In reality, this was a sexist statement made by a filmmaker, which led to him being fired. 2. The Science Fiction Screenplays. In general, SF scripts contain the following lines: –A female protagonist has been conceived;–manipulated into becoming so attached that she cannot leave;–manipulated into being in love with the main character;–manipulated into sexing up the story with inevitable sequel after sequel;–manipulated into mystery novels;–manipulated into videogames;–manipulated into movies; and so on. Any line that begins with 'N' – and ends with 'M' – is to be treated with contempt. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is to be taken as a challenge. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is to be considered a clue. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is to be TREATED WITH CONDUCT. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is to be REMEMBERED WITH CARE. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is to be SHRUNNED. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO MACHINARY. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO DUMB. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO IMPOSSIBLE TO IMPROVE. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOOARD. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO MUCH. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO MUCH AIDE. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO MUCH WORK. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO MANY LINES TO LOSE. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO MANY THINGS TO REMEMBER. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO MANY THINGS TO UNDERSTAND. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO MANY THINGS TO UNDERSTAND. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO MANY THINGS TO UNDERSTAND. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO MANY THINGS TO UNDERSTAND. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO MANY THINGS TO UNDERSTAND. Any line that begins with 'M' and ends with 'M' is TOO MANY THINGS TO UNDERSTAND. Human-robot interaction is a field that has been rapidly growing without much regulation. Notably, sex robots have been sold that look and sound exactly how the user wants. The implications of this are terrifying: customers have already begun ordering uncomfortably young-looking robots and are recreating rape scenarios, which is horrifying. There are obvious psychological effects that go along with this, but these have not been explored in any fashion. The film Blade Runner 2049 shows an artificial intelligence projected as a hologram that is intended to be a fully customizable romantic companion. Similar to sex robots, this raises the questions of what kind of ramifications this will have on people and ultimately on the human race. There was a marriage between a man in Japan and an artificial intelligence with no physical form. The most terrifying (and awesome) form of human-robot interaction is brain-computer interfaces. Initial development is aimed at aiding people with neurological disorders, but it will not take long for this to extend to cybernetic modifications on people with no disorders. Will this be regulated? Should this even be allowed? These are difficult questions to answer. 

Similar to BCIs, deepfakes are simultaneously terrifying and awesome. deepfakesare AIs that can replace images, videos, or audio of a person with another person of similar likeness. deepfakes began circulating in 2017, which were humorous at first, but the danger of Deepfakes quickly became apparent when (unsurprisingly), it went towards pornography. According to a study, a staggering 96% of deepfakesare pornographic, and started as deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films but quickly spread to revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. The widespread exploitation of deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes on the internet, and academic research has focused around detecting deepfakes. Some platforms, such as Facebook, instead have opted to enforce that users clearly note that media is a deepfakes. Some AIs are much more nuanced, and thus that much more dangerous. GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, is able to generate text so similar to that written by humans that they did not release it to the public out of fear that it would be rampantly misused. OpenAI has also released DALLE, a model that can generate artwork based on text prompts, which is a fun experiment, but could easily be misused.

Similar to BCIs, deepfakesare simultaneously terrifying and awesome. Deepfakes are AIs that can replace images, videos, or audio of a person with another person of similar likeness. deepfakesfirst began circuilating in 2017, which were humorous at first, but the danger of Deepfakes because apparent when (unsurprisingly), it went towards pornography. A staggering 96% of Deepfakes are estimated to be pornography Deepfakes. It didn’t take long to go from Deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films to creating revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. Deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes, and much of academic research has centered around being able to detect deepfakes. Multiple bills have been introduced to congress about deepfakes. GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, was able to generate text so human-like that the programmers did not open source the model out of fear of rampant misuse. OpenAI has also released a model called DALLE, which can generate artwork based on text prompts. This is a fun experiment but could easily be misused. 

One of the biggest issues with AI is that it is incredibly hard to relay these ideas to people outside academia, which stems back to the mythologization of AI. It is also imperative for those who use AI to be completely transparent about exactly what it is capable of and what it is using. There also needs to be an effort to educate people on what AI can do from a young age. This doesn’t have to be an effort to get more involved with AI, but moreso a rudimentary understanding of its limitations. 

One of the biggest issues with AI is that it is incredibly hard to relay these ideas to people outside academia, which is what leads to the difference between the perception and reality of AI. AI developers should be straightforward and honest about what is being developed, and there needs to be an effort to educate on what AI can do. AI tends to be a very mysterious field to those not in, but if the basics were taught, there would be a lot less misunderstanding about what AI can and cannot do.

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been gaining ground, but there are still many unanswered questions. Artificial Intelligence is often asked to perform specific tasks, such as scanning a specific population for disease, but there are also applications that go beyond just diagnosis. In the following paragraphs, we will explore a few of these more advanced applications. 

Boring’ Yet Important

One of the primary issues with AI is that it often does a poor job of what it tries. An AI for detecting cancer might find it difficult to distinguish between a human and a robotic patient, leading to the AI to suggest a robotic patient. This is not to say that there have not been any attempts to create intelligent AI; there have even beeings written about the problem of programming with AIs. However, these AIs tend to be very simplistic, and primarily intended for use in educational settings. The final major difference is that with AIs for games and data analysis, the goal is clearly defined: do you think this thing think like you do? Not necessarily. 

Human-robot interaction is a rapidly-growing field, and none of these AIs are without their flaws. In the following paragraphs, we will explore a few of these flaws. 

24/7/365: This could very well be the most important AIs argument of all time. Whether or not it is right or wrong, and whether it will have a significant impact on AI is currently in question. Any time something new is presented, it is often criticized for being too good to be true./MMH/NE/WC1UE was particularly well-suited to this criticism, as it showed that anything that was computationally simple could be implemented to be extremely complicated. It also opened the floodgates to the idea that anything that was not computationally simple could be reinterpreted to be more complex. This is generally referred to as OO because this is an application of what is called O(n), where n is the total number of possible operations that can be taken on an object. For instance, take the store and load functions from SQL Server. These were originally designed to be extremely simple to implement, but with the introduction of the millions of database connections that have been shipped, the op was adjusted to be anything that could be implemented in terms of database connections. This is especially true for the younger generations of AI, as simple operations such as indexing are no longer enough. Instead, algorithms such as gradient-based classifiers have begun to take over, which take examples from natural languages and train a neural network to recognize patterns. This is particularly exciting because it opens up a whole new world of application, as it allows for the creation of intelligent medical devices/dispensing organs, and ultimately the rehabilitation of severely injured soldiers. There are also applications which are purely theoretical, such as building diagnostics software, but which would obviously benefit from the knowledge that it could be implemented. 

Upcoming issues/limitations: This one is a bit more difficult to nail down. There are many different ways that AI can be misused, and many different applications can be served by different levels of implementation. For instance, there are applications which are all but impossible to ethically use AI for, such as self-driving cars, but which could absolutely use the training data to help find users who are best suited for the job. Similarly, there are applications which are incredibly obvious, but which could absolutely not be avoided. For instance, do we really want to have to store every restaurant in the US? This is a very hard question to answer, but is a good example that it is hard to anticipate how misuse of AI can lead to disastrous effects.

It didn’t take long to go from Deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films to creating revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. Deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes, and much of academic research has centered around being able to detect deepfakes. Multiple bills have been introduced to congress about deepfakes. Human-robot interaction is a field that has been growing at an alarming rate. Notably, sex robots have been sold that look and sound exactly how the user wants. The implications of this are terrifying: there are reports of customers asking for younger-looking robots and recreating rape scenarios, which is horrifying. The psychological effects of pursuing such a relationship with a robot has not been explored in any capacity, and it is currently a field that has no oversight. One of the best science fiction films, Blade Runner 2049 introduces the character Joi, an artificial intelligence which is projected as a hologram intended to be a fully customizable romantic companion. This has a similar issue with the sex robots: what kind of ramifications will this have on people, and ultimately the human race? A man in Japan married an artificial intelligence with no physical form. There are no laws governing this, and it is not a field many people have thought about. The psychological issues and ramifications of such a relationship have not been explored enough to make a decision on this yet. The most terrifying (and awe-inspiring) synthesis between humans and artificial intelligence is brain-computer interfaces. The initial development is meant to aid people with neurological disorders, but it will not take long for it to extend to cybernetic modifications on people. Will this be regulated? Should this even be allowed? At the risk of sounding like a Black Mirror episode, at what point does a human stop being human and start being a robot?

One of the primary issues is that artificial intelligence replaces menial labor. What do we do with the people who have suddenly become jobless? This will no doubt shift the job demand towards fields such as software engineering and robotics, but there will be notable disruptions in areas such as manufacturing and data entry. In short, any task that is simple enough to be learned by a computer will more than likely be taken over by a computer. However, there is the unanswered issue of how to redistribute the wealth generated by machines. Companies such as Alibaba and Amazon now have warehouses entirely staffed by robots. Should the money made by these warehouses go to the company? The workers? The government? This is a difficult question to answer, but a necessary one if we are to move forward.

There are also “narrow” AIs that are useful for a limited purpose. For example, IBM Watson was able to classify text documents into high and low-level categories. This application of artificial intelligence is known as “narrow” intelligent robotics. Other examples include Google’s DeepMind AI, which was able to defeat the world champion at Go, and IBM Watson 2.0, which was able to classify 20,000 text documents into high-level and low-level languages. These AIs have a limited scope of application, and it is important to realize that their contributions will not be of benefit to humanity.

Even when an AIs are useful, there are often practical concerns that need to be addressed. For example, how do we get people to buy space-age transportation? This might sound like a trivial question to ask,” but it is important to realize that’generalized transport system awareness will not be a trivial task. Furthermore, there are inherent conflicts of interest between attempting to improve the physical environment (by sending robots there) and sending robots there (by taking money for your work)? This is a good example that should teach us that’architectural–”idea. An AIs should not be able to think for itself,” and AnisIs have shown that they can.

It is important to realize that artificial intelligence is only one branch of science and that other branches as well, such as “weak” AI,” neural networks, and genetic algorithms, will take over in the not-too-distant future. In the meantime, focus on developing’technologies that are accurate and useful has the potential to yield revolutionary changes in the world of work.

Conclusion

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been gaining ground, but there are many questions that do not have an easy answer. It is important to realize that artificial intelligence is only one branch of science and that other branches as well, such as’narrow” intelligence, will take over in the not-too-distant future. In the meantime, focus on developing’technologies that are accurate and useful has the potential to yield revolutionary changes in the world of work.

Similar to BCIs, deepfakes are simultaneously terrifying and awesome. deepfakesare AIs that can replace images, videos, or audio of a person with another person of similar likeness. deepfakes began circulating in 2017, which were humorous at first, but the danger of Deepfakes quickly became apparent when (unsurprisingly), it went towards pornography. According to a study, a staggering 96% of deepfakesare pornographic, and started as deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films but quickly spread to revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. The widespread exploitation of deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes on the internet, and academic research has focused around detecting deepfakes. Some platforms, such as Facebook, instead have opted to enforce that users clearly note that media is a deepfakes. Some AIs are much more nuanced, and thus that much more dangerous. GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, is able to generate text so similar to that written by humans that they did not release it to the public out of fear that it would be rampantly misused. OpenAI has also released DALLE, a model that can generate artwork based on text prompts, which is a fun experiment, but could easily be misused.

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been surprisingly uninteresting to researchers. The main issue is that the typical AI is trained for extremely high-dimensional representations, which makes it easy to misclassify as AI. Furthermore, this AI often ends up being hostile, due to its habit of attacking its former students and employees (often with deadly results). It is important to realize that artificial intelligence is on the rise - just slower than the media coverage would lead you to believe.

There is a marked difference between the capabilities and expectations of Artificial Intelligence. Science fiction writers, film directors, and artists would have you believe that AI is manifested in sentient robots that are binary equivalents of humans. This kind of AI is referred to in academic literature as “strong” AI, which is an AI that is intelligent enough to understand or learn any intellectual task that a human being can. Generalized AI is not here yet -- instead, what you will find are “narrow” AIs that are trained to accomplish very specific tasks: identify an image, suggest an enjoyable movie, predict the next word in a sentence, etc. Narrow AI has been able to dethrone the world champion at Go, vanquish the Jeopardy champions, and defeat Gary Kasparov at chess. There are also “weak” AIs that can implement a limited part of a mind, but not the entire mind. The most common examples include Siri, Cortana, and Google Assistant: these voice assistants have a very narrow spectrum they can operate in, and asking any question outside of their limited scope will result in unhelpful responses. It is important to realize that artificial intelligence is on the rise - just slower than the media coverage would lead you to believe.

There is a marked difference between the perception and reality of Artificial Intelligence. Media is hyperfocused on “strong” AI, which is an AI that is intelligent enough to understand or learn any intellectual task that a human being can. This is the kind of AI glamorized in films and novels. In reality, AI today is much more boring. The majority of AI in production today is “narrow” AI, which are trained and fine tuned to perform extremely specific tasks. You may have heard of Google’s DeepMind AI, which dethroned the world champion at Go. IBM Watson dominated against the Jeopardy champions. These AIs are all narrow; they can only play the game they have been trained for. Furthermore, most AI found today is not nearly as exciting: data analysis, image classification, and signal processing. These applications do not attract media attention, but are incredibly important to their respective fields. The final major class of AI is “weak” AIs, which can implement a limited part of a mind, but not the entire mind. The most common examples include Siri, Cortana, and Google Assistant. These AIs have a very limited scope of operation, and asking any question outside of this scope will result in largely unhelpful responses. It is important to realize that artificial intelligence is on the rise - just slower than the media coverage would lead you to believe.

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been rapidly growing without much regulation. Notably, sex robots have been sold that look and sound exactly how the user wants. The implications of this are terrifying: customers have already begun ordering uncomfortably young-looking robots and are recreating rape scenarios, which is horrifying. There are obvious psychological effects that go along with this, but these have not been explored in any fashion. The film Blade Runner 2049 shows an artificial intelligence projected as a hologram that is intended to be a fully customizable romantic companion. Similar to sex robots, this raises the questions of what kind of ramifications this will have on people and ultimately on the human race. There was a marriage between a man in Japan and an artificial intelligence with no physical form. The most terrifying (and awesome) form of human-robot interaction is brain-computer interfaces. Initial development is aimed at aiding people with neurological disorders, but it will not take long for this to extend to cybernetic modifications on people with no disorders. Will this be regulated? Should this even be allowed? These are difficult questions to answer. 

Similar to BCIs, deepfakes are simultaneously terrifying and awesome. deepfakesare AIs that can replace images, videos, or audio of a person with another person of similar likeness. deepfakes began circulating in 2017, which were humorous at first, but the danger of Deepfakes quickly became apparent when (unsurprisingly), it went towards pornography. According to a study, a staggering 96% of deepfakesare pornographic, and started as deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films but quickly spread to revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. The widespread exploitation of deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes on the internet, and academic research has focused around detecting deepfakes. Some platforms, such as Facebook, instead have opted to enforce that users clearly note that media is a deepfakes. Some AIs are much more nuanced, and thus that much more dangerous. GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, is able to generate text so similar to that written by humans that they did not release it to the public out of fear that it would be rampantly misused. OpenAI has also released DALLE, a model that can generate artwork based on text prompts, which is a fun experiment, but could easily be misused.

Similar to BCIs, deepfakesare simultaneously terrifying and awesome. Deepfakes are AIs that can replace images, videos, or audio of a person with another person of similar likeness. deepfakesfirst began circuilating in 2017, which were humorous at first, but the danger of Deepfakes because apparent when (unsurprisingly), it went towards pornography. A staggering 96% of Deepfakes are estimated to be pornography Deepfakes. It didn’t take long to go from Deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films to creating revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. Deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes, and much of academic research has centered around being able to detect deepfakes. Multiple bills have been introduced to congress about deepfakes. GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, was able to generate text so human-like that the programmers did not open source the model out of fear of rampant misuse. OpenAI has also released a model called DALLE, which can generate artwork based on text prompts. This is a fun experiment but could easily be misused. 

One of the biggest issues with AI is that it is incredibly hard to relay these ideas to people outside academia, which stems back to the mythologization of AI. It is also imperative for those who use AI to be completely transparent about exactly what it is capable of and what it is using. There also needs to be an effort to educate people on what AI can do from a young age. This doesn’t have to be an effort to get more involved with AI, but moreso a rudimentary understanding of its limitations. 

One of the biggest issues with AI is that it is incredibly hard to relay these ideas to people outside academia, which is what leads to the difference between the perception and reality of AI. AI developers should be straightforward and honest about what is being developed, and there needs to be an effort to educate on what AI can do. AI tends to be a very mysterious field to those not in, but if the basics were taught, there would be a lot less misunderstanding about what AI can and cannot do.

According to a study, a staggering 96% of deepfakesare pornographic, and started as deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films but quickly spread to revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. The widespread exploitation of deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes on the internet, and academic research has focused around detecting deepfakes. Some platforms, such as Facebook, instead have opted to enforce that users clearly note that media is a deepfakes. Some AIs are much more nuanced, and thus that much more dangerous. GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, is able to generate text so similar to that written by humans that they did not release it to the public out of fear that it would be rampantly misused. OpenAI has also released DALLE, a model that can generate artwork based on text prompts, which is a fun experiment, but could easily be misused.

Similar to BCIs, deepfakesare simultaneously terrifying and awesome. Deepfakes are AIs that can replace images, videos, or audio of a person with another person of similar likeness. deepfakesfirst began circuilating in 2017, which were humorous at first, but the danger of Deepfakes because apparent when (unsurprisingly), it went towards pornography. A staggering 96% of Deepfakes are estimated to be pornography Deepfakes. It didn’t take long to go from Deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films to creating revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. Deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes, and much of academic research has centered around being able to detect deepfakes. Multiple bills have been introduced to congress about deepfakes. GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, was able to generate text so human-like that the programmers did not open source the model out of fear of rampant misuse. OpenAI has also released a model called DALLE, which can generate artwork based on text prompts. This is a fun experiment but could easily be misused. 

One of the biggest issues with AI is that it is incredibly hard to relay these ideas to people outside academia, which stems back to the mythologization of AI. It is also imperative for those who use AI to be completely transparent about exactly what it is capable of and what it is using. There also needs to be an effort to educate people on what AI can do from a young age. This doesn’t have to be an effort to get more involved with AI, but moreso a rudimentary understanding of its limitations. 

One of the biggest issues with AI is that it is incredibly hard to relay these ideas to people outside academia, which is what leads to the difference between the perception and reality of AI. AI developers should be straightforward and honest about what is being developed, and there needs to be an effort to educate on what AI can do. AI tends to be a very mysterious field to those not in, but if the basics were taught, there would be a lot less misunderstanding about what AI can and cannot do.

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been rapidly growing without much regulation. Notably, sex robots have been sold that look and sound exactly how the user wants. The implications of this are terrifying: there are reports of customers asking for younger-looking robots and recreating rape scenarios, which is horrifying. The psychological effects of pursuing such a relationship with a robot has not been explored in any capacity, and it is currently a field that has no oversight. One of the best science fiction films, Blade Runner 2049 introduces the character Joi, an artificial intelligence which is projected as a hologram intended to be a fully customizable romantic companion. This has a similar issue with the sex robots: what kind of ramifications will this have on people, and ultimately the human race? A man in Japan married an artificial intelligence with no physical form. There are no laws governing this, and it is not a field many people have thought about. The psychological issues and ramifications of such a relationship have not been explored enough to make a decision on this yet. The most terrifying (and awe-inspiring) synthesis between humans and artificial intelligence is brain-computer interfaces. The initial development is meant to aid people with neurological disorders, but it will not take long for it to extend to cybernetic modifications on people. Will this be regulated? Should this even be allowed? At the risk of sounding like a Black Mirror episode, at what point does a human stop being human and start being a robot?

GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, is able to generate text so similar to that written by humans that they did not release it to the public out of fear that it would be rampantly misused. OpenAI has also released DALLE, a model that can generate artwork based on text prompts, which is a fun experiment, but could easily be misused.

Deepfakes are AIs that can replace images, videos, or audio of a person with another person of similar likeness. deepfakesfirst began circuilating in 2017, which were humorous at first, but the danger of Deepfakes because apparent when (unsurprisingly), it went towards pornography. A staggering 96% of Deepfakes are estimated to be pornography Deepfakes. It didn’t take long to go from Deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films to creating revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. Deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes, and much of academic research has centered around being able to detect deepfakes. Multiple bills have been introduced to congress about deepfakes. Human-robot interaction is a field that has been thriving for over a decade, and has brought with it a host of disturbing developments. From the creation of mind controlled rats to the augmented androids AIs and Biohazards, science has only just begun to explore the implications of such a scenario. 

5) Big Data Science: This refers to the study of data sets of generalization, in which the goal is to collect as much data on individuals as possible, and to apply this data to individual differences to create race- or gender-specific advantage. The most prominent examples include GM crops and automated surgery. Wikipedia has a page dedicated to this, and it isn't pretty. Many articles on Big Data focus on applied problems such as data mining, but little else. This could be a huge mistake. In the following years, most AI will be superseded by systems that can do any task a human being can. This will be difficult to detect, and may not be welcomed by the public. This will be referred to as "big data" and referred to as "AI for humans" in publications. The best practice is for people to just accept that AI should do whatever a human being does is the standard. This will greatly reduce the number of reports of issues, and also open the door to much greater application of AI.

This is a long way from "imagine an AI that can play chess and you have an idea what you are looking at" to "imagine an AI that can play chess and you will understand me completely". This is a very realistic world, and it is entirely possible that the most common applications of AI will be Mindstorms-style brain-computer interfaces, and Personal Assistants. These are applications where the question of whether or not to allow AIs to be isomorphic with humans is immediately apparent. For example, consider IBM’s humanoid: is this a good use of corporate resources? Probably not, but it is the best they have. The same is probably not true for autonomous vehicles. mass’tweeting’is this a good use of our time? Probably. but only if it leads to something better.

There are also practical problems with attempting to force AIs to do anything humans can't. Most obvious is that this will create a world where AIs are used on a massive scale, and humanity is the only species that does not. Also, especially concerning is that this might lead to the emergence of a new class of superintelligent AI, which could be more palatable to the public than the real thing.

It is important to realize that artificial intelligence is on the rise - just slower than the media coverage would lead you to believe.

There is a marked difference between the perception and reality of Artificial Intelligence. Media is hyperfocused on “strong”AIs, which are the AIs that are said to be “strong”enough”toachieve any task a human would, on its own,. This is the kind of AI glamorized in films and novels. In reality, AI today is much more boring. The majority of AI in production today is “narrow”AIs, which are general‑purpose AIs that can be trained to do a limited task such as scan a room, pick a movie, or play a certain sound. This is the kind of AI most engineers are used to designing. The problem with “strong”AIs is that they are difficult to test, and puny returns on investment. Examples include “Watson”the IBM”personal assistant that was primarily intended to be used in education. This was actually an exercise in futility: the product turned out to be more about personality testing than anything else, and revealed too much about the student body to be of any use. The same can be said of Google’s Google Assistant: this was an extremely narrow application, and revealed too much about the student body to be of any use. The same can be said of Amazon’s Alexa: this was an extremely broad application, and led to disastrous results. The same can be said of IBM’s humanoid AI: this was an extremely limiting construct, and led to disastrous results. Notably, Tesla’s humanoid robot was intended to be a game changer: it was meant to be a fully customizable robot, and was meant to be the standard operating procedure for robots in the future. The final model was an incomprehensible mess, and proved to be too difficult to learn. 

Even though we don’t have general AI, there has already been a marked increase in the amount of work that goes into preparing that AI. This is particularly important when it comes to machine translation: it is extremely hard to anticipate all the ways in which an AI could be misused. In the following years, we will see a marked increase in the percentage of jobs that are completely automated. This is widely viewed as a

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been gaining ground in recent years, but there are many unanswered questions that will need to be addressed in order to bring about any degree of widespread human-robot interaction. 

 Up until now, we have only been discussing the issues with narrow and weak AIs, but inevitably, general AI will eventually be developed. The problem of control rises up: if AIs are sentient (and seeing how we model everything after humans, they more than likely will be), will they come to resent us? Science fiction certainly thinks so. How do we ensure that sentient AI will not decide to fight back? There will undoubtedly be discussion of giving robots rights, which is a much more complex matter altogether, and none of these have any clear answers. 

 Up until now, we have only been discussing the issues with narrow and weak AIs, but inevitably, general AI will eventually be developed. How do we control these AIs? It is entirely possible that AI decides to fight back if it is capable of realizing that it is serving humans. Furthermore, this might lead to the push to give AI rights, which is a complex matter without a clear answer.

At the same time, this could very well be the most important field in human-robot interaction in the not-too-distant future. Human-robot interaction is a field that has been rapidly growing without much regulation. Notably, sex robots have been sold that look and sound exactly how the user wants. The implications of this are terrifying: there are reports of customers asking for younger-looking robots and recreating rape scenarios, which is horrifying. The psychological effects of pursuing such a relationship with a robot has not been explored in any capacity, and it is currently a field that has no oversight. One of the best science fiction films, Blade Runner 2049 introduces the character Joi, an artificial intelligence which is projected as a hologram intended to be a fully customizable romantic companion. This has a similar issue with the sex robots: what kind of ramifications will this have on people, and ultimately the human race? A man in Japan married an artificial intelligence with no physical form. There are no laws governing this, and it is not a field many people have thought about. The psychological issues and ramifications of such a relationship have not been explored enough to make a decision on this yet. The most terrifying (and awe-inspiring) synthesis between humans and artificial intelligence is brain-computer interfaces. The initial development is meant to aid people with neurological disorders, but it will not take long for it to extend to cybernetic modifications on people. Will this be regulated? Should this even be allowed? At the risk of sounding like a Black Mirror episode, at what point does a human stop being human and start being a robot?

Similar to BCIs, deepfakes are simultaneously terrifying and awesome. deepfakesare AIs that can replace images, videos, or audio of a person with another person of similar likeness. deepfakes began circulating in 2017, which were humorous at first, but the danger of Deepfakes quickly became apparent when (unsurprisingly), it went towards pornography. According to a study, a staggering 96% of deepfakesare pornographic, and started as deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films but quickly spread to revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. The widespread exploitation of deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes on the internet, and academic research has focused around detecting deepfakes. Some platforms, such as Facebook, instead have opted to enforce that users clearly note that media is a deepfakes. Some AIs are much more nuanced, and thus that much more dangerous. GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, is able to generate text so similar to that written by humans that they did not release it to the public out of fear that it would be rampantly misused. OpenAI has also released DALLE, a model that can generate artwork based on text prompts, which is a fun experiment, but could easily be misused.

Deepfakes are AIs that can replace images, videos, or audio of a person with another person of similar likeness. deepfakesfirst began circuilating in 2017, which were humorous at first, but the danger of Deepfakes because apparent when (unsurprisingly), it went towards pornography. A staggering 96% of Deepfakes are estimated to be pornography Deepfakes. It didn’t take long to go from Deepfaking celebrities into pornographic films to creating revenge porn, fabricating clips of people saying things they didn’t, and financial hoaxes. Deepfakes led to DARPA funding a project to detect deepfakes, and much of academic research has centered around being able to detect deepfakes. Multiple bills have been introduced to congress about deepfakes. GPT-3, a text generation AI developed by OpenAI, was able to generate text so human-like that the programmers did not open source the model out of fear of rampant misuse

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been ambitiously pursued by a select few. The initial applications are in the medical field, where humanoid robots will be used to diagnose and combat mental illness. The final-trader applications include energy production and robotics education. The initial-mover advantage is that humanoid robots are easier to train and maintain than humanoids, which will lead to an explosion in medical-research into humanoid robots. This will in turn lead to the commercialization of humanoid robots in factories and other jobs that do not require a lot of cognitive ability. The issue of exploitation is complicated by the fact that most humanoid robots are not intended to be worked with: they are primarily for entertainment purposes, and geek culture is a particularly fertile ground for exploitation. The final-mover advantage to this line of research is that it will lead to the commercialization of humanoid robots in factories and other jobs that do not require much cognitive ability. This will in turn lead to the rise of a new field of cognitive robots: industrial robots with no formal education or training. This will lead to a marked increase in employment opportunities for humans with no formal education or training, and a marked decrease in employment opportunities for humans with no such qualification. 

One of the primary issues is that artificial intelligence will disrupt menial jobs. What do we do with the suddenly jobless people? This is a hard question to answer, but should absolutely be addressed if we are to move forward. A keystone of any economic system should be employment: employment allows a society to function, and a society that does not provides any sort of return is not sustainable. Moreover, this returns we get are in the form of increased income for the 1%, which is simply not enough. Any form of taxation is simply not high enough. Raising the minimum wage to $15 an hour is a good example of why.

Human-robot interaction is a field that has been pursued with varying degrees of success. The main issues include lethality, personality alteration, and conflict of interest. One of the most egregious examples of a man-robot interaction was the infamous lab-rat incident, in which rats were implanted with mind-reading transhumanist robots and raised as human beings. This has a distinct human element to it, as the robots begin as people with complex needs and desires, and begin to fulfill these needs. This is a complex and controversial field to master, but could have a profound impact on human-robot interaction in general. C.V.A. A.I. is a field that has been attempted but has not yet been successful. The main issue with A.I. is that it is difficult to control. An A.I. that is sentient (and sentient enough to want to live independently) would be a game-changer, but such a thing has not been attempted. Instead, the main force for AI improvement in A.I. is cognitive: model training, classification, and AI fluency. This is the section where I recommend books on AI that teach you how to program, not how to code. The majority of AI in production today is written by people with no formal education in AI, and most of these AIs are not very good. Even relatively simple AIs can greatly improve on the performance of the human race, and this will not happen without a massive education push. Microsoft’s Twitter chatbot was meant to engage in conversation with twitter users, and it only took one day for the internet to teach it to be misogynistic, racist, and anti-semitic. The potential is there, and it will take a massive education effort to make it to the surface. B.AI.B. is short for "brain-inspired interface". This is an obvious attempt to push artificial intelligence through the brain, but it ends up backtracking and becoming an AI for B.A.B.A.! ============ ============ [Brief Summary Of] ============ [Table Of Contents] [Next Chapter] [Discuss] ================================ [Brief Summary Of] ================================ [Table Of Contents] [Next Chapter] [Discuss] ================================ [Brief Summary Of] ================================ [Table Of Contents] [Next Chapter] [Discuss] ================================ How To Program - A Practical Guide By William Shatner (Almost) Complete [Brief Summary Of] ================================ [Table Of Contents] [Next Chapter] [Discuss] ================================ [Brief Summary Of] ================================ [Table Of Contents] [Next Chapter] [Discuss] ================================ [Brief Summary Of] ================================ [Table Of Contents] [Next Chapter] [Discuss] ================================ Language Understanding - The Secret To Finding & Creating Highly Accurate Sentences In A Multilingual World By Ryan Holiday (Almost) Complete [Brief Summary Of] ================================ [Table Of Contents] [Next Chapter] [Discuss] ================================ [Brief Summary Of] ================================ [Table Of Contents] [Next Chapter] [Discuss] ================================ Generalized AI - Generalized AI and the Psychology Of Good People Convinced They Are Good By K.J.
